              <span id="reviewTextContainer357977093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer82514019947289809">What an unsettling little book! I stayed up late last night to finish it and I awoke this morning with it still on my mind (and I think I dreamed about it too). Octavia Butler is skilled at making me re-examine my beliefs about humanity.<br/><br/>The Oankali are interesting and somewhat threatening aliens. Their evolutionary history seems to have come from the echinoderm or cnidarian branches of the tree of life and their appearance is initially terrifying to any human. Our protagonist, Lilith, has to be </span>
  <span id="freeText82514019947289809" style="display:none">What an unsettling little book! I stayed up late last night to finish it and I awoke this morning with it still on my mind (and I think I dreamed about it too). Octavia Butler is skilled at making me re-examine my beliefs about humanity.<br /><br />The Oankali are interesting and somewhat threatening aliens. Their evolutionary history seems to have come from the echinoderm or cnidarian branches of the tree of life and their appearance is initially terrifying to any human. Our protagonist, Lilith, has to be conditioned and altered biochemically in order to interact with them. Their motivations are very opaque and they are in no hurry to reveal them.<br /><br />Once again, Butler is exploring the nature of power dynamics, with the Oankali having the upper hand in the relationship, setting all the rules. Humans are treated like lab animals, like livestock, and like pets, although by the end of the book there are complications that cannot completely be explained by those relationships. However, the new relationship still feels very exploitative.<br /><br />Also examined is the matter of genetic change—how much alteration can be done to a genome before you say that a species has been altered to become a new species? Is survival worth such a transformation? How much would I be willing to endure merely to survive?<br /><br /><i>Dawn</i> asks many more questions than it provides answers to and I will be most interested to read the second and third installments in the series.<br /><br />Book 213 in my science fiction and fantasy reading project.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="82514019947289809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary " href="/user/show/27528763-gary">Gary </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer865848216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14381565661401893487">Okay. So how do I describe this really weird sci-fi book that masquerades as horror. Not hunt you down alone on a ship Alien horror, more like subtly psychologically really disturbing (to me anyway) sci-fi.<br/>The basic situation is a girl, Lilith, (for mythology fans, please note the symbolism) is the lone survivor of a nuclear holocaust and is left with the responsibilities of awakening the other humans from a deep sleep, telling them they are on an alien ship, leading them to earth, and, of cours</span>
  <span id="freeText14381565661401893487" style="display:none">Okay. So how do I describe this really weird sci-fi book that masquerades as horror. Not hunt you down alone on a ship Alien horror, more like subtly psychologically really disturbing (to me anyway) sci-fi.<br />The basic situation is a girl, Lilith, (for mythology fans, please note the symbolism) is the lone survivor of a nuclear holocaust and is left with the responsibilities of awakening the other humans from a deep sleep, telling them they are on an alien ship, leading them to earth, and, of course, convincing them that the deal she struck with the aliens to get them back is a nasty but good idea.<br />It's hard to get more in depth with this story without spoiling anything. Let's just say sympathies were with the people that thought it was a good idea to kill the protagonist and her bunch.<br />I normally have a cast iron stomach regardless of how brutal what I am reading is. For some reason I felt nauseous often when reading this, especially when I began to realize the extent of the relationship between Lilith and the aliens.<br />Overall, I can clearly see why this book is so highly rated. I am not sure I want to complete the trilogy. I found myself skimming and not really liking or caring about any of the characters. It is well written and for the right reader it's a gem, I am sure. I would be tempted to go right to the end of book three, figure out what happens, and go read something else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14381565661401893487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText11620603065699122944" style="display:none">Somehow my reread created a 2nd entry for this book. I erased it. 2/16/20<br /><br />This is the first novel I ever read by Octavia Butler. I'm now a grandmother but when I read this my daughter was 6 months old. I still have the paperback with the white woman on the cover. LOL! Imagine my surprise when the main character was a statuesque black woman, extremely capable, practical and a natural leader. OB has been my favorite author ever since.<br />This novel was published in 1987 and some of the politics and technology are dated. This deals with a future in which a nuclear holocaust has laid waste to the Earth. Western nations were especially hard hit. Lilith Iyapo is studying in South America when the crisis happens. She survives the initial explosion and is rescued. Her rescuers are not anything she could've ever imagined. The Oankali are the most unique aliens I have ever read about. They travel thorough space in a living ship looking for mates and are as much our captors as our rescuers.</span>

<div id="review_647548574" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/647548574" />
    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424631975p2/2490110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/647548574?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi">Mimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781453263679" href="/book/show/15844625-dawn">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone looking for well-written thoughtful sci-fi</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mimi by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=my-kindle">my-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer647548574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9791969663074565010"><i>Dawn</i> begins with Lilith Iyapo awakening in solitary confinement. She later learns she's on a living space ship, held as a captive by the oankali, an alien race. There had been a war several years ago on Earth that destroyed the planet and almost wiped out the human race. A few survivors were rescued and brought to the ship. All were healed but left sedated for the time being; a select few will be awoken, like Lilith, once it’s time to return to Earth and resettle the planet.<br/><br/>There’s a catch thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText9791969663074565010" style="display:none"><i>Dawn</i> begins with Lilith Iyapo awakening in solitary confinement. She later learns she's on a living space ship, held as a captive by the oankali, an alien race. There had been a war several years ago on Earth that destroyed the planet and almost wiped out the human race. A few survivors were rescued and brought to the ship. All were healed but left sedated for the time being; a select few will be awoken, like Lilith, once it’s time to return to Earth and resettle the planet.<br /><br />There’s a catch though, several in fact, which are revealed as the story unfolds. The main one being, for humans to return to Earth, they must accept a genetic trade with the oankali. Meaning that, if humans want to repopulate the planet, they will only bear human-oankali children. This will play out more fully in the next book, <i>Adulthood Rites</i>. <br /><br />Lilith, being the most resilient and trustworthy human, is handed the task of teaching and training the other humans to survive in the wilderness of new Earth. The rest of the story is about the many challenges the humans face as they practice surviving on new Earth and the dilemmas Lilith face alone as she helps this group in their struggles.<br /><br /><i>Full review of the trilogy <a href="http://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2014/09/24/review-xenogenesis-trilogy-liliths-brood-by-octavia-butler/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9791969663074565010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1257945495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257945495" />
    <a title="Lilia Ford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10992009-lilia-ford"><img alt="Lilia Ford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381027796p2/10992009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257945495?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lilia Ford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lilia Ford" href="/user/show/10992009-lilia-ford">Lilia Ford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257945495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1168908393752474499">I sought this out deliberately as the best way I could think of to protest this year's Hugo Award debacle, though I wasn't sure I'd like it since it definitely falls closer to the "speculative" end of the sci-fi spectrum than what I usually read--or enjoy. Well, so much for that worry. I couldn't put it down. I mean that literally: I was supposed to go out to dinner and I ended up cancelling so I could finish it. I totally get why it's so acclaimed: the set up is bracingly original, and the look</span>
  <span id="freeText1168908393752474499" style="display:none">I sought this out deliberately as the best way I could think of to protest this year's Hugo Award debacle, though I wasn't sure I'd like it since it definitely falls closer to the "speculative" end of the sci-fi spectrum than what I usually read--or enjoy. Well, so much for that worry. I couldn't put it down. I mean that literally: I was supposed to go out to dinner and I ended up cancelling so I could finish it. I totally get why it's so acclaimed: the set up is bracingly original, and the look it takes at issues such as assimilation, difference, xenophobia, adaptation, colonization, appropriation, and the Oankali idea of "trade," is crazily complex and nuanced, never content to rely on the old political certitudes, liberal or conservative, that you'd expect. The Oankali's thesis that humanity is genetically driven to self-destruct due to "intelligence in the service of hierarchy" is one of those concepts that whole seminars in college could be spent debating. <br /><br />Fascinating as all of this is, the reason I loved, loved this book is Lilith Iyapo. Every now and then you encounter a character that you passionately wish was part of your own life, and she was it--I wish she was my aunt, which is funny because she's quite a bit younger than I am. But I wish I'd had a woman in my life like this when I was younger. I think it's her profound adaptability mixed with something hard and uncompromising. Those words sound like contradictions: Lilith showed they're not. There's a ruthless bluntness and unwillingness to indulge in lies or self-delusion which forces her to carry on even when she's staring failure in the face. <br /><br />"How many times can you have everyone taken from you and still have the will to start again?" Tate muttered.<br />As many times as it took, Lilith thought wearily. <br /><br />Also:<br />She had learned to keep her sanity by accepting things as she found them, adapting herself to circumstances by putting aside the old ones whose memories might overwhelm her.<br /><br />Butler is in a way offering her as the model of a human being who could transcend our drive to self-destruct. But her picture of this character goes beyond "ordinary guy/gal" heroism, since arguably Lilith's effectiveness is that she is not heroic--she lacks anything like charisma or the ability to inspire and lead people; she also lacks the optimism or hopefulness or romanticizing idealism that usually drive "heroic" behavior. Even before the apocalypse, she'd survived the death of her child and husband, and she is nothing if not pessimistic. Her virtue is that she copes--she sees reality, that which can truly not be changed by wishful thinking, and deals with it. That clarity of vision means that she can recognize her own fear, and by doing so, not act on it--one of the few humans in the story capable of that. That brand of stoicism seems to me to be inextricably tied to her experience as a woman, and yet to have nothing of the usual socially sanctioned notions of desirable/lovable "feminine" behavior--these are rare enough qualities in real life, and extremely hard to find in books also. As I said, I wished I'd had a female relative like this in my life when I was younger. I'll have to make due with Butler's portrayal. <br /><br />Luckily for me and everyone, this is one of those rare books where a fictional character seems to achieve that level of vital presence that can fool our brains into reacting to them as if they were real people. There was no woman quite like this in my past, but there is now, and my ideas of humanity, of what it means to be a woman, of strength, of heroism will be reshaped accordingly. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1168908393752474499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_962147534" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/962147534" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/962147534?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=sword-and-laser">sword-and-laser</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer962147534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7390229080022854820"><b>Executive Summary:</b> A well written and very different story that just made me uncomfortable the whole time. It wasn't exactly my type of book, but it may be yours.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>These sorts of reviews are the hardest to write. For books I love, the reviews usually come pretty easily. For books I don't, I try to express why I didn't like the book without ranting about it and then move on and don't worry too much about the quality of the review.<br/><br/>This book falls somewhere in between. It really made m</span>
  <span id="freeText7390229080022854820" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> A well written and very different story that just made me uncomfortable the whole time. It wasn't exactly my type of book, but it may be yours.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />These sorts of reviews are the hardest to write. For books I love, the reviews usually come pretty easily. For books I don't, I try to express why I didn't like the book without ranting about it and then move on and don't worry too much about the quality of the review.<br /><br />This book falls somewhere in between. It really made me feel uncomfortable the entire time. I'm sure that was the point. Not only the way the Oankali treated Lilith, but the way the other humans treat her.<br /><br />The story was interesting and certainly made me think a lot more than most of the books I usually read. Not only is it well written, but Ms. Butler somehow packs a whole lot of story and ideas into such a short book without making it feel rushed or incomplete.<br /><br />She's obviously a great writer. That said that level of discomfort is not something I enjoyed, and I read for enjoyment. I kind of want to see where this story goes next, but I'm still not sure if I'll continue on with the series or not.<br /><br />That said, I'm glad I finally read a book by Ms. Butler and may try another of her books in the future if I don't decide to continue on to the next in this series. From the sounds of it though, working these sort of issues of discrimination and subjugation is a common thing for her work, so she simply may not be an author for me.<br /><br />If you like books that challenge you to think though, this may be a great choice for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7390229080022854820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1707842107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1707842107" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/155663-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581956036p2/155663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1707842107?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/155663-david">David</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to David by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4086118-michael">Michael</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/155663-david?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1707842107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12749624356222501625">Although I have read a lot of science fiction, I had never even heard of Octavia Butler before reading this book. But I am so glad that I read it, and the next two books of the Xenogenesis series. <br/><br/>This is an excellent sci-fi novel about Lillith, a young woman in the after-days of a nuclear apocalypse on Earth. She is one of a few survivors, just barely alive, picked up by an alien race in a spacecraft. She is brought back to health, but kept in almost total isolation. She is pretty much clueless</span>
  <span id="freeText12749624356222501625" style="display:none">Although I have read a lot of science fiction, I had never even heard of Octavia Butler before reading this book. But I am so glad that I read it, and the next two books of the Xenogenesis series. <br /><br />This is an excellent sci-fi novel about Lillith, a young woman in the after-days of a nuclear apocalypse on Earth. She is one of a few survivors, just barely alive, picked up by an alien race in a spacecraft. She is brought back to health, but kept in almost total isolation. She is pretty much clueless as to where she is, who her rescuers are, and why they are keeping her in such isolation. She communicates with the aliens remotely, without actually seeing them. There is virtually no way for the aliens to show their faces, without upsetting her.<br /><br />The aliens are here to "trade". It is unclear at first what they want to trade with humans, and I will not reveal the answer here. But it is clear that Octavia Butler has thought up a completely self-consistent story for the aliens, and why they have come to Earth. <br /><br />The aliens maneuver Lillith to act on their behalf, to awaken other humans aboard the spacecraft. Her task is to explain to the situation to newly awakened humans. She realizes that if she chooses the wrong humans to awaken at first, the results may be disastrous.<br /><br />This is a short sci-fi novel, and it sets the stage for the following two in the Xenogenesis series. You really need to read the three novels in order, to get a full understanding of the objectives of the aliens, and the dangerous situation they have placed Lillith in. And the dangers continue throughout the entire series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12749624356222501625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_954253394" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/954253394" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10165256-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340093730p2/10165256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/954253394?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer15577405741220331069">Fascinating from so many points of view! Beautifully written and deeply insightful. I can't think of any other book I've read that tells a similar story and I found this a very unique tale which was brilliantly told. <br/><br/>This was my first <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/29535.Octavia_E__Butler' title='Octavia E.   <span id="freeText15577405741220331069" style="display:none">Fascinating from so many points of view! Beautifully written and deeply insightful. I can't think of any other book I've read that tells a similar story and I found this a very unique tale which was brilliantly told. <br /><br />This was my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/29535.Octavia_E__Butler" title="Octavia E. Butler" rel="nofollow noopener">Octavia E. Butler</a> and it more than lived up to all the wonderful things I'd heard about her work. The insights into human nature are too plentiful to list, made without seeming to try. The aliens are striking and just so alien. One of the best examples of the insight into human nature comes early in the book when the protagonist meets her first alien. I prefer not to include spoilers in my reviews, but you'll know what I mean when you read it, which you should. <br /><br />The journey Lilith takes throughout the course of the novel is deep and convoluted and entirely engaging. It isn't always easy to read, but then I think that truth rarely is. <br /><br />I found this an unusual book, not altogether enjoyable, but undeniably powerful. I highly recommend it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6900184930076958762">I was afraid to start the Xenogenesis trilogy because I knew there’d be issues with consent. Some reviewers described it as graphic, horrific, disturbing—and they were right on all accounts, but Dawn wasn’t as graphic as I’d initially feared. That’s not to say it was an easy book to read. The Oankali violate personal boundaries, both physical and mental, and genuinely believe their actions service humanity. The Oankali strip Lilith of her right to her mind, her body, and a life of her choosing. </span>
  <span id="freeText6900184930076958762" style="display:none">I was afraid to start the Xenogenesis trilogy because I knew there’d be issues with consent. Some reviewers described it as graphic, horrific, disturbing—and they were right on all accounts, but Dawn wasn’t as graphic as I’d initially feared. That’s not to say it was an easy book to read. The Oankali violate personal boundaries, both physical and mental, and genuinely believe their actions service humanity. The Oankali strip Lilith of her right to her mind, her body, and a life of her choosing. What’s most disturbing is Lilith’s eventual acceptance of the Oankali. The reader has to wonder if Lilith made this decision on her own terms, or if the Oankali’s neurochemical manipulations led her to feeling the way she did. I’ll end by saying that Dawn ends on a very disturbing note. I was horrified as I read the final pages.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2871764841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2871764841" />
    <a title="Allison Hurd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd"><img alt="Allison Hurd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530670583p2/14495279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2871764841?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison Hurd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison Hurd" href="/user/show/14495279-allison-hurd">Allison Hurd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=authors-of-color">authors-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=fem-author">fem-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-2019-challenge">sff-2019-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14495279-allison-hurd?shelf=sff-bookshelf">sff-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871764841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1730911279970982317">Dawn was certainly my favorite of the three Butler books I've now read, but that's not as strong praise as I'd like it to be. I think she's imaginative and does a good job making everyone else feel her discomfort. But it feels a lot like that uncomfortable position at holiday dinners where you want to tell Grandma she can't say that, but you know you can't do that because then your discomfort will be a family feud and it's just not worth the fight. So, I think this is likely to be my last Butler</span>
  <span id="freeText1730911279970982317" style="display:none">Dawn was certainly my favorite of the three Butler books I've now read, but that's not as strong praise as I'd like it to be. I think she's imaginative and does a good job making everyone else feel her discomfort. But it feels a lot like that uncomfortable position at holiday dinners where you want to tell Grandma she can't say that, but you know you can't do that because then your discomfort will be a family feud and it's just not worth the fight. So, I think this is likely to be my last Butler attempt.<br /><br /><b>CONTENT WARNING</b>: I mean it's Butler, shields up for every goddamn thing, but in particular (no actual spoilers, just a list of topics) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ slavery, rape, coercion of will, medical experimentation, loss of a loved one, misogyny, anyone with aversions to writhing/skittering things and/or holes or bumps be warned <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Things that were fascinating:</u><br /><br />-<b>The aliens</b>. Jesus flipping crow, they were uuuuncomfortably different. I grew to like two of them, but woof that was a lot of work. It was amazing how she was able to make me viscerally uncomfortable with the aliens and wary of them, their intentions, and their culture. Incredibly well done.<br /><br />-<b>The premise</b>. Again, so very unsettling and real feeling. What would you do if you woke up and found that Earth was no more? How would you react?<br /><br />-<b>The Butler-bits</b>. She has a style, doesn't she? A Black woman with a grudge in a system with extremely uneven power balances who is so incredibly pissed off and scared at her position but who tries to make the best of it? Oh yeah. This just screams Butler's message with every sentence. "What do you want me to do about it, fix yourself," feels like the subtext in just about every conversation.<br /><br /><u>Things that made it clear I can't keep doing this:</u><br /><br />-<b>The viewpoints</b>. I am uncomfortable with a lot of her apparent world views or thought experiments. Real spoilers and possible controversy in the tag. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ In all of the books of hers I've read, she seems to imply that the only real rape is violent rape, and everything else is a choice. With every fiber of my being I abhor this idea to the point that I can't interact with the ideas around it. Furthermore, she seems to suggest that the "ideal" or perhaps "uninhibited" society is polyamorous and bisexual. While I absolutely agree that there are lots of people who are poly and/or bi/pan and I want them to have the same protections and happiness I enjoy, I don't think that gay or straight people are affecting their sexual or romantic attraction simply for society's sake. And I also don't think we'd all be happier with multiple partners. Again, this is a strong reaction from me. I appreciate representation of different family groups and sexualities, but well, you know, respect all people and relationships etc. etc. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This might just be a personal reaction, but I avoid people in real life who tell me these things, and I think I'm done with it in the fictional space, too. <br /><br />There are also some conclusions about the violence and instability of people that...while I can't say I disagree that people are violent and unstable, I can say I don't think it'd go like this, or that I didn't believe the set up for them to be like this.<br /><br />-<b>Narrative structure</b>. There really isn't one. She writes what sounds good and eventually comes to the end of the thought experiment. A meandering, slow, conceptual book can be good, but only if the concepts and characters are intriguing. This did better than Fledgling or Wild Seed for me, but I'm not sold.<br /><br />-<b>The characters</b>. I'd say I liked Nikanj, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ it's a rapist.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Everyone else felt either too distant or too bitter for me to latch on to. I felt their emotions, and the emotions I felt were that these were deeply unhappy people who were only continuing on because of the instinct for self preservation. <br /><br />In the end it was quick, it was uncomfortable, and it had some bits I liked, which is what I guess Ms. Butler thinks sex is for all of her characters, at least, and now I'm done trying this relationship. I think she's a marvelously imaginative, prolific and important author and I also think I have the gist now and can move on with a clear conscience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1730911279970982317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4waWdiSKC8ImwU0SL9Ie//jKOPUvGhDShaKzFBHE7IGy+wpOzl927Tfsy3q0tE3bxcoa6GvgxklCe85+PdUSUQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3834279491364541683">Octavia Estelle Butler was an American science fiction writer, one of the best-known among the few African-American women in the field. She won both Hugo and Nebula awards. In 1995, she became the first science fiction writer to receive the MacArthur Foundation "Genius" Grant.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1008111-dawn">Quotes from Dawn</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You have a mismatched pair of genetic characteristics. Either alone would have been useful, would have aided the survival of your species. But the two together are lethal. It was only a matter of time before they destroyed you."<br /><br /> [...]<br /><br />Jdahya made a rustling noise that could have been a sigh, but that did not seem to comer from his mouth or throat. "You are intelligent," he said. "That's the newer of the two characteristics, and the one you might have put to work to save yourselves. You are potentially one of the most intelligent species we've found, though your focus is different from ours. Still, you had a good start in the life sciences, and even in genetics."<br /><br />"What's the second characteristic?"<br /><br /> "You are hierarchical. That's the older and more entrenched characteristic. We saw it in your closest animal relatives and in your most distant ones. It's a terrestrial characteristic. When human intelligence served it instead of guiding it, when human intelligence did not even acknowledge it as problem, but took pride in it or din not notice it at all..." The rattling sounded again.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>

          </div>
